< text>
Things sure changed after finishing college a decade ago, starting my career and then having twin sons. One BIG change was my exercise regimen and my body fat! I tried indoor fitness classes, lifting weights and running on treadmills but something was missing...fortunately, for me and hopefully you, I found it at ZogSports! It came down to being outside in beautiful LA, connecting with other people and playing fun sports under the sun. I've played soccer and volleyball for the past year and have grown friendships and decreased my fat while building muscle, endurance and stamina. I highly recommend ZogSports here in LA and around the country. To top it all off, Zog donates money to a charity of your team's choice if you win the season. Great company, great people and great to stay in shape. What are you waiting for?</text>

Each venue/gym we play at seems to have their own set of refs, meaning some places the refs like to call more fouls, another place the refs let the games be a little more free flowing with less calls, nonetheless, all fun and games.

<Review>At this point, I've participated in five or six seasons of beach volleyball with Zog.  I've met some great people - several of whom I now play with regularly.  I've found that the league has a really good balance of being competitive-but-not-too-competitive and social.  The only issue I've run into is that the league could sometimes do a better job of evaluating players to ensure they're being placed at the right level.  Especially in a sport like beach volleyball, one or two weak players (relative to the rest of the team) can leave a team non-competitive for a whole season, so that's something to look out for.  With that in mind, I suggest, if possible, finding reliable folks at your level of play and forming a team with them, that way you know who you'll be playing with heading into the season.  In any case, my experience with Zog has been great.  I look forward to my games every weekend, and expect to play in their leagues for many more seasons going forward.  Oh, and Casey, Zog's GM for LA, does an excellent job and has always been super responsive when I've reached out with random questions.  In general, their staff has been very positive in my interactions with them.< /Review>< Resp>

<userid>112723086743496071396</userid>< Name>
Sean Magee</Name>
<Date>1528140376247< /Date>< rate>
1</rate>
< Text>
TL;DR  Multiple 3 team leagues, poor communication, missing/late refs

3-team leagues are really a bummer. You play a double header every other week against the same people, and eventually people get tired of it, which results in forfeits nearly every week. I made the mistake of signing up for 2 Zog leagues at the same time (flag football and soccer), and it turned out that they both only had enough players for 3 teams.

Here's a pretty good snapshot of how disorganized Zog is:  During Week 2 of my Hollywood Friday night soccer league, there was no ref. Afterwards, we went to the bar that's partnered with the league (you get deals on drinks). The manager at the restaurant literally asked, "What's Zog?" He had no idea what we were talking about.

The league contact, Jeffrey Hajek, hardly replies to any emails. I sent him 4 emails asking to put me in touch with another Zog representative to talk about the 3-team league issue, and he never did. Four emails.

My best advice is to do LASportsnet or Clubwaka. If you need to do Zog, be sure to ask how many people are in the league before you sign up. If they don't tell you, or something seems a little off, don't sign up.

Maybe Zog is better in Santa Monica, but in Hollywood, it's pretty bad.

*****As a disclaimer, the Hollywood Basketball league is actually great (run by Barbara Davis). Great refs, plenty of teams, and well-organized. Other than that, I wouldn't do any Zog sport in the valley.< /Text>

< Text>
If you want to play for fun and you are not overly competitive this is the league for you. As for myself I have played competitive softball pretty much all my life not to mention i have played in college too so I find the level of competiveness a little on the weak side. I have met some cool people and they do give some money to charity so that's a good thing. Not sure how much goes to them but at least they donate. I think that's their motto, playing for a cause since their league fees are super expensive.

There a few things I dislike about the league. One is that they claim that we have a sponsor but never get anything from the sponsor. So how is that sponsorship? Not sure about that one. I would usually not say anything about it but they put the sponsor on the shirts that WE pay for. Shouldn't we decide if we want the sponsor logo on our shirts or not? What happens if we don't like the sponsor ? haha anyway...

Second thing I dislike is that some of the umpires are new never had experience umping a game. They train them which is fine but are not completely aware of the rules. This causes a lot of conflicts between teams of who is right an who is wrong.

Lastly, this is a 'for profit' organization so the fees are pretty high compared to other leagues. This league only has seven games plus playoffs. If you don't mind paying that then give it a GO.

Hope this helps...< /Text>

<Date>1527965331524< /Date><Rating>4< /Rating>< text>
Been coming here for years now. It‚Äôs the local ‚Äúcheers‚Äù bar in Tierrasanta where every one knows your name ... the drinks are cheap here! $3.50 well drinks and many beers to choose from - draft or bottle. They have mini pitchers which is the way to go. Good bar food .. $2.00 taco Tuesdays and 50 cent wings on Thursdays. Their burgers are the best. The crowd here can vary depending on the time of day. Most of the locals from the neighborhood are here earlier in the day through happy hour. (Happy hour is 7 am - 7 pm).  They are a special group of really nice people ranging from early 20‚Äôs up to 85 yo! After 8 pm is when the much younger crowd files in. They have a band every Friday night with no cover. Pool tables, dart board and music!!  Weekends used to be for football and was a blast but sadly they decided not to renew their football package so you‚Äôre stuck watching whatever happens to be televised on a local channel. This is a fun local dive with great prices.</text>

I recently moved to Tierrasanta and I drive by JP's everyday.  I was a little discouraged to go in because there are always lot of bikers out in front and seemed like a much older crowd.  It was a random tuesday night and a friend and I decided to go in and check it out.  Surprisingly, it was larger than I expected with pool tables and a karaoke section. < Review>
Some reviews are hard, but this one is easy. There aren't enough stars to do justice to a practice that excels in every way. I'm 71 yrs old an over my life I'm been a patient of some talented dentists but Dr. Scherer is in a class of his own. He'd be a huge success in NYC or L.A. or any major city. And the support staff is amazing truly empathic and friendly. I remember Siskel and Ebert and I'll say the same. Two thumbs up, way up.
Because of a med that I was taking I lost 5 or 6 teeth and both jawbones were infected. But the repairs are nearly complete now. I believe that good health requires good teeth. It's a mystery to me how Tuolumne County attracted a world class dentist. It's probably the lifestyle here and natural beauty of Sonora. There's Yosemite, the High Sierras, fishing, skiing and mountaineering plus the proximity to Cities like San Jose and San Francisco. That's what drew me when I moved here. I've never given ten stars because there's no 11. I'll give 5 stars, but I'd like to give 9 out of ten.
JIM D.  Sonora, CA< /Review>
